============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG23)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P
Candidate formulas: 53

Let \(P\) be the only effective variable in the GT (since GT has no \(t\)-dependence). First rewrite the GT into a simple canonical form.

### Ground Truth (fixed function)
\[
0.5980421691(1-\tfrac{P}{32.9394024023})P \;+\; 0.5980421691(1-e^{-0.07682777496P})P
\]
Expand:
- First part: \(0.5980421691P - 0.5980421691\frac{P^2}{32.9394024023}\)
- Second part: \(0.5980421691P - 0.5980421691P e^{-0.07682777496P}\)

So GT is exactly
\[
\boxed{GT(P)= A\,P^2 + B\,P + C\,P\,e^{kP}}
\]
with
- \(A = -0.5980421691/32.9394024023 \neq 0\) (negative),
- \(B = 2\cdot 0.5980421691 \neq 0\),
- \(C = -0.5980421691 \neq 0\),
- \(k = -0.07682777496 \neq 0\).

So any matching candidate must be able to represent **simultaneously**: a \(P^2\) term, a linear \(P\) term, and a \(P\exp(kP)\) term (with nonzero coefficient), and must have **no extra functional forms** (no constants, no pure \(\exp(kP)\) without \(P\), no \(\log\), no \(|P|\), no \(1/(P+\cdot)\), no \(t\)-dependence, etc.), unless those can be set to zero by parameter choices.

---

## Candidate-by-candidate analysis

### 1.
\(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2/(c3 e^{Pc4+c5}+1) + Pc6 + c7 e^{Pc8} + c9\)  
Has a logistic-type term \(P/(a e^{bP}+1)\) which cannot equal \(P e^{kP}\) for all \(P\). Also has optional pure exponential \(c7e^{Pc8}\) and constant \(c9\). Even setting those to 0, the logistic term cannot become \(P e^{kP}\). **No.**

### 2.
\(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 e^{Pc3} + P^{c4}c5 e^{Pc6} + c7\)  
To match GT, we’d need the extra \(P^{c4} e^{Pc6}\) term to vanish: set \(c5=0\). Also set \(c7=0\). Then we have \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 e^{Pc3}\), which matches GT’s structure exactly by choosing \(c0=A,\; c1=B,\; c2=C,\; c3=k\). **Yes, match possible.**

### 3.
Includes \(P c2 (c3|P|)^{c4}\) and \(|P|\) makes it non-analytic/sign-dependent unless forced off. Setting \(c2=0\) removes it, leaving \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc5 e^{Pc6} + Pc7 + c8\). But GT needs \(P e^{kP}\), not \(e^{kP}\) without \(P\); here it is \(P*c5*exp(P*c6)\) actually yes that part is fine, but there is also an extra \(Pc7\) and constant \(c8\) which can be set to 0, and \(Pc1\) already covers linear. Wait: after setting \(c2=0\), we have \(P^2c0 + P(c1+c7) + P c5 e^{Pc6} + c8\). Set \(c8=0\). This can match GT by choosing \(c0=A\), \(c1+c7=B\), \(c5=C\), \(c6=k\). So **Yes, match possible** (the \(|P|\) term can be eliminated).

### 4.
\(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 e^{Pc3} + P^{c4}c5 + c6\)  
Even if \(c6=0\) and \(c5=0\) to remove \(P^{c4}\), we get \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 e^{Pc3}\) (missing the required factor \(P\) multiplying the exponential). Cannot make \(Pc2 e^{Pc3}\) from \(c2 e^{Pc3}\) for all \(P\). **No.**

### 5.
Has Max(0, P+const) piecewise terms; GT is smooth/analytic. Only way is to zero those coefficients: set \(c1=0\) and \(c6=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + Pc3 + Pc4 e^{Pc5} + c8\). Set \(c8=0\). This matches GT form with \(c0=A\), \(c3=B\), \(c4=C\), \(c5=k\). **Yes.**

### 6.
Contains \(\log(Pc5+1)\) which GT doesn’t have; must set \(c4=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 e^{Pc3} + c6\). Still has \(e^{Pc3}\) without \(P\). Not match. **No.**

### 7.
\(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 e^{Pc3} + c4 e^{Pc5} + c6\)  
Even setting \(c4=0,c6=0\), still has \(Pc2 e^{Pc3}\)? No: it is \(P*c2*exp(P*c3)\) actually yes: expression says \(P*c2*exp(P*c3)\) plus \(c4*exp(P*c5)\). If set \(c4=0,c6=0\), we get \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2 e^{Pc3}\), exactly GT form. **Yes.**

### 8.
Has \(P\log(\cdots)\) term; must set \(c4=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2 e^{Pc3} + c7\). Set \(c7=0\). Matches. **Yes.**

### 9.
Has \(P^2 c1/(c2+|P|)\) non-polynomial unless \(c1=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + P(c3) + P c4 e^{Pc5} + c6\). Set \(c6=0\). Matches. **Yes.**

### 10.
Has \(P*c4/(c5+|P|)\) unless \(c4=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2 e^{Pc3} + c6\). Set \(c6=0\). Matches. **Yes.**

### 11.
Has rational terms \(P*c4/(Pc5+c6)\) and \(c7/(Pc5+c6)\). To remove, set \(c4=0,c7=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2 e^{Pc3} + c8\). Set \(c8=0\). Matches. **Yes.**

### 12.
\(P^2c0 + Pc1 + c2 e^{Pc3} + c4 e^{Pc5} + c6\)  
Exponentials are not multiplied by \(P\). Cannot become \(P e^{kP}\) for all \(P\). **No.**

### 13.
Has extra constant \(c4\) and a complicated \(c5\exp(\sin(\log(\cdot)))\) term. Must set \(c5=0\) and \(c4=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2 e^{Pc3}\). Matches. **Yes.**

### 14.
Similarly, set \(c5=0\) and \(c4=0\). Remaining \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2 e^{Pc3}\). Matches. **Yes.**

### 15.
\(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2 e^{Pc3}\)  
Exactly the GT functional family. Choose \(c0=A,\;c1=B,\;c2=C,\;c3=k\). **Yes.**

### 16.
Uses \(|P|\): \(P c0|P| + Pc1 + P c2 e^{c3|P|}\). GT has \(P^2\) (which equals \(P|P|\) only for \(P\ge 0\), not all real \(P\)). Also exponential depends on \(|P|\), not \(P\). Cannot match for all real \(P\). **No.**

### 17.
\(P c0|P| + P c1 e^{Pc2} + Pc3\). Same \(|P|\) issue for \(P^2\). **No.**

### 18.
\(P c0|P| + Pc1 + c2 e^{Pc3}|P|\). Wrong absolute value structure. **No.**

### 19.
\(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2 e^{Pc3} + c4\). Set \(c4=0\). Matches. **Yes.**

### 20.
\(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + P c3 e^{Pc4} + Pc5 + c6\). Combine \(P^2\) and \(P\) coefficients; set \(c6=0\). Then matches by choosing \(c0+c1=A\), \(c2+c5=B\), \(c3=C\), \(c4=k\). **Yes.**

### 21.
\(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2 e^{Pc3} + Pc4 + c5\). Set \(c5=0\). Linear term is \(P(c1+c4)\). Matches. **Yes.**

### 22.
Has \(P*c4*Max(0,P+c5)\) piecewise unless \(c4=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2 e^{Pc3} + c6\). Set \(c6=0\). Matches. **Yes.**

### 23.
Has \(P*c2/(P+c3)\) and also pure exponentials \(c4 e^{Pc5}+c6 e^{Pc7}\) (not multiplied by \(P\)). Even zeroing some, the remaining forms can’t produce exactly \(P e^{kP}\) without extra terms. **No.**

### 24.
Has \(P*c2/(P+c3)\) and also \(P*c4 e^{Pc5}\) plus pure exponential \(c6 e^{Pc7}\). You could set \(c2=0,c6=0,c8=0\), leaving \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c4 e^{Pc5}\), but then you’re missing the independent linear term? Actually \(Pc1\) is there, so it matches if we also need \(P^2\): yes \(P^2c0\) present. So with \(c2=0,c6=0,c8=0\), it matches GT by mapping \(c0=A,c1=B,c4=C,c5=k\). **Yes.**

### 25.
Contains \(t\)-dependent sine term; must set its amplitude \(c5=0\) and also constant \(c4=0\). Then reduces to candidate 15. Matches. **Yes.**

### 26.
Has \(c4\sin(Pc5+c6)\); must set \(c4=0\), and \(c7=0\). Then matches. **Yes.**

### 27.
Has explicit \(t\)-dependence via \(e^{c1 t}\), \(t^2\), \(t\). Only way is set \(c1=0,c6=0,c7=0\). Then becomes \(P^2c0 + P(c2+c5) + P c3 e^{Pc4} + c8\). Set \(c8=0\). Matches. **Yes.**

### 28.
Has \(c4 t\); must set \(c4=0\) and \(c5=0\). Then matches. **Yes.**

### 29.
Has \(P*c4*(c5+t)^{c6}\) which depends on \(t\) unless \(c4=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P c2 e^{Pc3} + c7\). Set \(c7=0\). Matches. **Yes.**

### 30.
Has pure \(c2 e^{Pc3}\) (no \(P\) factor) and a \(t\)-dependent sinusoidal term. Even setting sinusoid off (\(c5=0\)) and constant \(c4=0\), still cannot turn \(c2 e^{Pc3}\) into \(P e^{kP}\). **No.**
